The control flow graph for the source code is as follows:

  • The start of the graph is the function AnalyzeCode.
  • The code flows from AnalyzeCode to RemoteService to perform the code analysis.
  • If there is an error during the code analysis, the flow goes to the Error block.

graph TD;
style Start fill:#228B22, stroke:#000000, stroke-width:2px;
style PrimaryPath fill:#228B22, stroke:#000000, stroke-width:4px;
style ErrorPath fill:#B22222, stroke:#000000, stroke-width:2px;

Start-->AnalyzeCode;
AnalyzeCode-->CheckServiceStatus;
CheckServiceStatus-->{
    ServiceOnline[Service is online?]
    ServiceOffline[Service is offline]
}
ServiceOnline-->{
    AnalyzeSourceCode[Analyze source code]
    DisplayResults[Display analysis results]
}
ServiceOffline-->{
    DisplayErrorMessage[Display error message]
}
AnalyzeSourceCode-->{
    SendRequest[Send request to remote service]
    ReceiveResponse[Receive response from remote service]
}
SendRequest-->ReceiveResponse;
ReceiveResponse-->{
    Success[Response is successful?]
    Error[Response is an error]
}
Success-->{
    ParseResponse[Parse response]
    DisplayResults
}
Error-->{
    LogError[Log error]
    DisplayErrorMessage
}

The control flow graph above represents the control flow of the analyzed source code. The primary path is highlighted in green, representing the main flow of the code. The error path is highlighted in red, representing the flow when an error occurs.

The control flow starts at the "AnalyzeCode" function, which is the entry point for analyzing the source code. It then proceeds to check the status of the remote service by calling the "CheckServiceStatus" function. Depending on the status of the service, the control flow branches to either the "ServiceOnline" or "ServiceOffline" blocks.

If the service is online, the code proceeds to analyze the source code by sending a request to the remote service and receiving a response. The control flow then branches based on the success or error status of the response. If the response is successful, the code parses the response and displays the analysis results. If the response is an error, the code logs the error and displays an error message.

If the service is offline, the code directly displays an error message without attempting to analyze the source code.

The control flow graph for the provided source code is as follows:

  • The starting point is the Start node.
  • From the Start node, the control flow goes to the analyzeCode node.
  • From the analyzeCode node, there are two possible paths:
    • The control flow goes to the remoteServiceCall node.
    • The control flow goes to the handleError node.
  • From the remoteServiceCall node, the control flow goes to the displayResults node.
  • From the handleError node, the control flow also goes to the displayResults node.

The primary path through the code is from the Start node to the analyzeCode node, then to the remoteServiceCall node, and finally to the displayResults node. This path represents the successful execution of the code.

The alternate path is from the Start node to the analyzeCode node, then to the handleError node, and finally to the displayResults node. This path represents the error handling flow of the code.
